Mutual Oath in Division Disputes: Hanafi vs. Maliki
Ruling on mutual oath in a division dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutual oath in a division dispute, explain its qiyas to a sale price dispute, and contrast it with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
When a share is disputed after division, Hanafi applies mutual oath; possession does not determine ownership.

After a division of jointly owned property, a partner may claim that a specific item in the other's hand is actually his share and was not delivered. The other partner denies. How does the law resolve this? The Hanafi school uses mutual oaths (taḥāluṯ) and rescinds the division for that item, analogizing to a dispute over the price in a sale. The Maliki school instead believes the possessor. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: when one partner claims a specific item in the other's hand is his undelivered share and the other denies, both take oaths (taḥāluṯ) and the division is rescinded for that item.
This is found at the beginning of the passage.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Maliki school holds that the person in possession (the one holding the item) is believed on oath, so the item remains with him.
The text mentions 'عند مالك: القول لصاحب اليد'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Maliki view is based on the principle that the defendant (possessor) takes an oath and his statement is accepted, as he is the one being sued.
The Hanafi response counters that neither is purely plaintiff or defendant.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the dispute is symmetrical: each partner claims the same property, so neither is a simple plaintiff. They analogize to a dispute over the price in a sale before delivery, where mutual oaths are used. This qiyas justifies the mutual oath.
The passage also addresses an objection about qiyas after possession, but the conclusion is to accept mutual oath despite it being against qiyas in some respects.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi, if both swear, the division is rescinded for that item; in Maliki, the item stays with the possessor after his oath.
This directly affects the outcome of such disputes in court.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وادعى أن ذا حظه ولم يسلم إلي و كذبه شريكه تحالفا، وفسخت القسمة في ذلك. ذا حظه أشار به إلى ما في يد صاحبه. (عيني) وفسخت القسمة: لأن الاختلاف فيما يحصل له بالقسمة، فصار نظير الاختلاف في المبيع والثمن، وعند مالك: القول لصاحب اليد ولا يخفى أنه يبدأ بيمين أيهما شاء. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۳۰۷/۸] ولقائل أن يقول: التحالف في البيع فيما إذا كان قبل القبض على وفاق القياس كما علم في محله، أما بعد القبض فمخالف للقياس لكن عرفناه في البيع بالنص وهنا أيضا التحالف مخالف للقياس؛ لأن كلا منهما ليس مدعيا ولا يمكن أن يقاس على التحالف في البيع بعد القبض؛ لما تقرر أن ما على خلاف القياس لا يقاس عليه غيره ولا يمكن إلحاقه بطريق دلالة النص؛ لأن القسمة ليست في معنى البيع من كل وجه؛ إذ فيها معنى الإفراز والمبادلة معا فليتأمل في الجواب. (تكملة بتغيير)
And if one claims that this is his share and it was not delivered to him, and his partner denies him, they take oaths (mutual oath) and the division is rescinded in that. (Commentary: 'This is his share' refers to what is in the hand of his partner. (Ayni) And the division is rescinded because the dispute is about what he obtained through the division, so it becomes analogous to a dispute regarding the sale price. According to Malik, the word is given to the person in possession, and it is well known that the oath begins with whichever one wishes. Tuhfat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/307. And it can be said: mutual oath in sale occurs before taking possession as per analogy, as is known in its place; after taking possession it is contrary to analogy, but we know it in sale by textual evidence. Here too mutual oath is contrary to analogy, because neither of them is a plaintiff, and it cannot be analogized to mutual oath in sale after possession, because it is established that what is contrary to analogy cannot be analogized to something else, and it cannot be attached by way of indication of the text, because division is not equivalent to sale in every respect, since it contains both the meaning of separation (ifraz) and exchange (mubadala) simultaneously. So one should reflect on the answer.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where after division, one partner points to a specific property in the other's hand and claims, 'This is my share, it was not given to me.' The other partner denies this. The Hanafi ruling is that they perform mutual oaths (taḥāluṯ) and the division is rescinded with respect to that property. The reasoning is that the dispute is about what each obtained through the division, similar to a dispute between buyer and seller over the price or the goods in a sale contract. The commentary notes that Imam Malik holds the opposing view that the person in possession is believed. The passage also addresses a potential objection: mutual oaths in sale are only analogically valid before possession; after possession, they are contrary to analogy but permitted by explicit text. Can the same be applied to division? The answer is that division is not exactly like sale because it involves both separation (ifraz) and exchange (mubadala), so the text does not analogize it perfectly, and one must seek a proper answer.

Key Terms
تحالف (taḥāluṯ): Mutual taking of oaths by both parties in a dispute, each swearing to their claim.
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens when one partner claims a specific property in the other's hand is his share and the other denies, after division?
A) The claim is dismissed because the division is final.
B) The person in possession takes an oath and keeps the property.
C) Both parties take mutual oaths and the division is rescinded.
D) The divider's testimony is sought to resolve the dispute.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a dispute over a specific share after division is resolved by mutual oaths and rescission, not by defaulting to the possessor.

Gross Disparity in Division: Right to Rescission
Ruling on dissolution of division due to gross disparity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ghubn fahish, distinguish it from ghubn yasir, state the Hanafi ruling on rescission in both judge-ordered and mutual consent divisions, and explain the tarjih within the school.

Core Idea
Gross disparity in division voids the contract – consent does not cure injustice.

When co-owners divide shared property, the law requires a fair apportionment. If it later emerges that one party received a severely undervalued share, the division may be overturned. This lesson explores the Hanafi concept of 'gross disparity' (ghubn fahish), its definition, and the crucial dispute over whether mutual consent can waive the right to rescission.

Guided Path
1
Define ghubn fahish
Identify the definition: a disparity beyond the normal margin of appraiser estimation, e.g., value appraised at 2000 but actually 1000.
The threshold is roughly half the value or more.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Division by judge's order vs division by mutual consent. Note the consensus for judge-ordered division.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf
For mutual consent, some early Hanafis said no rescission due to consent and analogy to sale. Others said rescission because condition of justice missing.
The latter is the correct view.
4
Apply the tarjih
The relied-upon position is rescission in both cases. Authors of al-Kafi, Qadi Khan, and later authorities settled this.
Fatwa is upon rescission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ظهر غبن فاحش في القسمة تفسخ، ولو استحق بعض شائع من حظه، بعد القسمة رجع كنصف ما في يده المستحق منه. [الشرح: ولو ظهر إلخ : أي لو ظهر غبن فاحش في القسمة وهو الذي لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين بأن قوم بألفين، فظهر أن قيمته ألف، تفسخ القسمة مطلقا، سواء كانت القسمة بقضاء القاضي أو بالتراضي على الأصح، وبيانه: أنه إذا ادعى الغلط في التقويم بأن قال: إن قيمة هذا أقل مما قومتموه، فإن كان مقدار الغلط غبنا يسيرا وهو الذي يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين، لا يصح دعواه، ولا يلتفت إليه، وإن كان غبنا فاحشا، فإن كانت القسمة بقضاء القاضي، فسخت القسمة اتفاقا؛ لأن تصرف القاضي مقيد بالعدل والنظر، ولم يوجد وإن كانت بالتراضي، فقد قيل: لا يلتفت إلى قول مدعيه؛ لأن دعوى الغبن لا تعتبر في البيع، فكذا في القسمة؛ لوجود التراضي، وقيل: تفسخ؛ لأن شرط جوازها و لم توجد، ند، فوجب نقضها، وهو الصحيح، ذكره في "الكافي"، قال في "العناية : وهو الصحيح، وعليه الفتوى. قال في "رد المحتار": قال المصنف في "المنح": والصحيح المعتمد ما قدمناه من "الكافي" و"قاضي خان"، وبه جزم أصحاب المتون، وصححه أصحاب الشروح، وبه أفتيت مرارا. (ملتقط من الكتب)
And if a gross disparity (ghubn fahish) appears in the division, it is rescinded. And if some undivided property from his share is reclaimed after division, he recovers like half of what is in his hand from which the claim is made. [Commentary: And if a gross disparity appears, i.e. a disparity that does not fall within the valuation of appraisers, such as if the property was valued at two thousand and then appears to be worth one thousand, the division is rescinded absolutely, whether the division was by a judge's order or by mutual consent according to the sound view. The explanation: when one claims an error in valuation by saying that the value of this is less than what you appraised, if the amount of error is a slight disparity that falls within the valuation of appraisers, his claim is not valid and is ignored. If it is a gross disparity, then if the division was by a judge's order, it is rescinded by agreement because the judge's action is constrained by justice and consideration, and that was not present. If it was by mutual consent, some said his claim is not considered because a claim of disparity is not considered in sale, so similarly in division due to the presence of mutual consent. Others said it is rescinded because the condition for its permissibility was not present, so it must be overturned. This latter view is correct, as mentioned in al-Kafi. Al-Inaya says: it is correct and fatwa is upon it. Radd al-Muhtar says: the author of al-Munah said: the correct and relied-upon view is what we presented from al-Kafi and Qadi Khan, and the authors of the matns firmly held it, and the authors of the commentaries validated it, and I have given fatwa accordingly many times.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of a significant disparity in value that appears after division. A 'gross disparity' (ghubn fahish) is one that is beyond the normal margin of error in appraisal, e.g., the property is worth half of what it was appraised at. In such a case, the division is rescinded regardless of whether it was executed by a judge or by mutual agreement, according to the sound opinion. For slight disparities, the claim is ignored. When the division is by a judge, there is consensus on rescission because the judge's duty is to ensure justice. For mutual consent divisions, there was a difference of opinion: some argued that since one consented, the claim of disparity is not heard, similar to sale where ghubn does not give a right of rescission. However, the correct view, which is the basis of fatwa, is that the division is rescinded because the fundamental condition of fair division was missing.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghubn fahish): A gross disparity in value that is beyond the normal margin of estimation, typically half the value or more.
تقويم المقومين (taqwim al-muqawwimin): Valuation made by professional appraisers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The division stands because both parties consented.
B) The division is rescinded because the condition of fairness was missing.
C) The division is rescinded only if the judge ordered it.
D) The party claiming disparity must prove fraud.

Key Takeaway
A gross disparity (ghubn fahish) in division of property invalidates the division, even if the parties mutually consented, because inequitable division is against the required justice.

Reclaiming an Undivided Share After Division: The Hanafi Intra-Madhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division validity after reclamation of an undivided share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on whether division is dissolved when an undivided part of a partner's share is reclaimed, and identify the operative ruling (Abu Hanifa's view).

Core Idea
A reclaimed undivided share in one partner's portion does not invalidate the entire division; the affected partner has options.

After a division of jointly owned property, if it turns out that a third party had a claim on an undivided part of one partner's new share, does the division collapse? The Hanafi school has a nuanced position based on the nature of the reclaimed property (specific vs. undivided) and whether it concerns the whole or a part. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute on this question, with Imam Abu Hanifa holding that the division remains valid and the partner may seek compensation or demand a new division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the exact situation: two partners divide property equally; after division, an undetermined part of one partner's share is reclaimed by a third party.
The reclaimed part is 'some undetermined' (ba'd sha'i') within the share, not a specific item.
2
Distinguish three cases of reclamation
The passage explains three scenarios: (a) specific part of a share – consensus no dissolution; (b) undivided part of the whole property – consensus dissolution; (c) undivided part of one share – disputed.
Only case (c) is the subject of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi positions
Know each imam's stance: Abu Hanifa – division not dissolved, partner has options; Abu Yusuf – division dissolved; Muhammad – inconsistent reports.
The matn presents Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon ruling.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the affected partner can claim proportional compensation from the other partner's share or return the remainder and redivide. Under Abu Yusuf, the division must be restarted entirely.
This difference impacts judicial practice: preserving vs. voiding the division.
5
Apply to similar scenarios
Contrast the disputed case with the agreed cases: if reclaimed part is specific, division stands by consensus; if undivided share of whole, division dissolved by consensus.
This helps internalize the criteria for when dissolution occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض شائع إلخ: يعني إذا تمت القسمة وأفرز نصيب كل واحد من الشريكين، ثم استحق بعض غير معين في نصيب أحدهما بأن كانت الدار بينهما نصفين واستحق نصف نصيب أحدهما، المستحق فيه بقسطه أي وهو ثمن جميع الدار على شريكه، ولا تفسخ القسمة يعني جبرا على المستحق منه شاء أو لم يشأ، بل له الخيار إن رجع بذلك في نصيب صاحبه، وإن شاء رد ما بقي واقتسما ثانيا، وظاهر عبارة المصنف وإن كان يوهم أن عدم الفسخ حتم واجب، لكن المراد ما بيناه وهذا المذكور من عدم الفسخ قول الإمام. والتفصيل: أن الاستحقاق إما أن يكون في بعض معين أو شائع، وعلى الثاني إما أن يكون في بعض شائع في الكل أو في أحدهما، ففي الصورة الأولى لا تفسخ القسمة إجماعا، سواء كان في نصيب أحدهما أو كليهما؛ لأن ما وراء المستحق بقي مفرزا على حاله ليس للغير فيه حق، ويرجع على شريكه بحسابه، وفي الصورة الثانية تفسخ اتفاقا، وفي الصورة الثالثة شاء نصيب رجع بربع نصيبه مسألة الكتاب - لا تفسخ عند أبي حنيفة، وتفسخ عند أبي يوسف، وقول محمد مضطرب، - وهي =
'Some undivided property etc.': Meaning when the division is complete and the share of each of the two partners is separated, then some undetermined (undivided) part of the share of one of them is reclaimed, such as if a house was divided equally between them and half of the share of one of them is reclaimed. The reclaimed property is recovered in proportion to its share, i.e. one-eighth of the entire house from the partner. And the division is not dissolved, meaning it is not forced upon the one from whom it was reclaimed, whether he wishes or not. Rather, he has the option: either he can claim compensation from his partner's share, or he can return what remains and they divide again. The literal wording of the author might give the impression that non-dissolution is obligatory, but the intended meaning is what we have explained. This non-dissolution is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. The detailed ruling: The reclamation either relates to a specific part or an undivided part. In the latter case, either it is an undivided part of the whole property or of one share. In the first scenario (specific part), the division is not dissolved by consensus, whether the reclamation is from one share or both, because what remains beyond the reclaimed property remains separated in its state with no right of others to it, and the partner recovers from his partner proportionally. In the second scenario (undivided part of the whole), the division is dissolved by agreement. In the third scenario (undivided part of one share), according to Abu Hanifa, it is not dissolved; according to Abu Yusuf, it is dissolved; and the statement of Muhammad is inconsistent. And this is the case of the book.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where after division, it turns out that part of the property given to one partner actually belonged to a third party (or was subject to a claim). The ruling depends on whether the reclaimed property was a specific part (mu'ayyan) or an undivided share (sha'i'). If it was a specific part of a specific share, there is consensus that the division is not dissolved; the partner whose share was reduced is compensated proportionally from the other partner's share. If the reclaimed property was an undivided share of the entire original property, the division is dissolved completely by agreement. The disputed case is where the reclaimed property is an undivided share of just one partner's share. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the division is not dissolved, and the affected partner has the option to seek compensation or demand a new division. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the division is dissolved. Imam Muhammad's view is reported inconsistently. This dispute is the subject of the chapter (mas'alah al-kitab).

Key Terms
بعض شائع (ba'd sha'i'): An undivided part or share of property, as opposed to a specific designated part (mu'ayyan).
استحقاق (istihqaq): Reclamation of property from someone's possession by proving rightful ownership or claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an undivided part of one partner's share is reclaimed after division, what is the ruling on the division?
A) The division is dissolved by force.
B) The division is not dissolved, but the partner has the option to seek compensation or demand a new division.
C) The division is dissolved only if the reclaimed part is more than half.
D) The division stands with no recourse for the affected partner.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the effect of reclamation after division depends on whether the reclaimed property is specific or undivided, and if undivided, whether it affects the whole or one share; for an undivided part of one share, the division is not dissolved and the partner has options.

Division Not Rescinded When a Third Party's Right Appears in One Share
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qismah and istihqāq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling regarding the effect of a third party's claim (istihqāq) on a completed division (qismah) when the claim pertains to a common share in only one partner's portion, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A third party's claim limited to one partner's share does not invalidate the division; the partner compensates from his own property.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi school regarding division of joint property. When a division is completed and later a third party proves ownership of a part that was common in one partner's share, does the division collapse? The scholars of the school differ, and this passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the arguments of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, with the relied-upon position being that of Abu Hanifa. By understanding this dispute, you will grasp how the purpose of qismah (tamayyuz and ifrāz) governs the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Read the scenario: after a division (qismah) is completed, a third party appears claiming ownership of a part that was common (shā'i') in the share of only one partner. The central question is whether this claim rescinds the division or is resolved by compensation.
Note that the claim is not on a specific item but on a common fraction within one partner's portion.
2
Contrast Abu Hanifa's and Abu Yusuf's positions
Abu Hanifa holds the division stands; the partner who conveyed the claimed share must compensate the third party from his own property. Abu Yusuf argues the division should be rescinded because a new partner appears without consent, similar to claiming a common part in the whole property.
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) jointly support Abu Hanifa's position in this passage, though Abu Yusuf's individual view is recorded.
3
Analyze the qiyas arguments
Abu Hanifa analogizes to a situation where two partners divide property that is partially owned by a third: if the front half is shared with a third and the back half is only between them, they can validly divide such that one gets a share of the front and a quarter of the back. This shows that division is not nullified by a third party's interest confined to one segment. Abu Yusuf analogizes to istihqāq of a common part in the whole, which would rescind division because the third party's share would be split across both shares.
The key distinction is whether the claim affects both shares (harm to third) or only one (no harm).
4
Determine the tarjih
The commentator declares Abu Hanifa's view as al-aṣaḥḥ (most correct). The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that if a claim appears in one partner's share, the division remains valid, and compensation is given; under Abu Yusuf's view, the division would be rescinded entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقسطه في حظ شريكه، ولا تفسخ القسمة، ولو تمايئا أي ربع نصيبه بعد القسمة = والأصح أنه مع أبي حنيفة، لأبي يوسف: أن بالاستحقاق ظهر شريك آخر، والقسمة بدون رضاه لا تصح، فصار كما لو استحق بعض الشائع في الكل، بخلاف المعين؛ لأن ما وراء المستحق بقي مفرزا على حاله ليس للغير فيه حق. ولهما: أن المقصود بالقسمة التمييز والإفراز، ولا ينعدم باستحقاق جزء شائع في نصيب أحدهما، ولهذا جازت القسمة على هذا الوجه في الابتداء بأن كان النصف المقدم مشتركا بينهما وبين ثالث والنصف المؤخر بينهما لا شركة لغيرهما فيه، فاقتسما على أن لأحدهما ما لهما من المقدم، وربع المؤخر يجوز، فكذا في الانتهاء، وصار كاستحقاق شيء معين، بخلاف الشائع في النصيبين؛ لأنه لو بقيت القسمة لتضرر الثالث بتفرق نصيبه في النصيبين، أما ههنا فلا ضرر بالمستحق فافترقا فافهم واحفظ. هذا ما لخصته من الشروح وغيرها.
By his share in the lot of his partner, and the division is not rescinded, and if they mutually shared, meaning a quarter of his share after division. And the most correct is that (the ruling) is with Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf: through the claim, another partner appears, and division without his consent is not valid, so it becomes like when a part of the common property is claimed in the whole, unlike a specific (item); because beyond the claimed item, the rest remains separated as it is, with no right of another in it. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the purpose of division is distinction and segregation, and it is not nullified by the claim of a part that is common (shā'i') in the share of one of them. For this reason, division in this manner is permissible at the outset: if the front half is common between them and a third, and the back half is between them without a third, and they divide such that one takes what both have in the front and a quarter of the back, it is permissible. So too at the conclusion. And it becomes like the claim of a specific thing, unlike when the common part is in both shares; because if the division were to remain, the third would be harmed by the dispersion of his share across two shares. Here, there is no harm to the claimant, so they are distinct. Understand and memorize. This is what I have summarized from the commentaries and others.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding what happens when a third party's right (istihqāq) appears after a division (qismah) has been made. The base matn states: 'ولو تمايئا' meaning 'if they mutually shared' (a portion after division). The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa holds that the division is not rescinded; rather, the partner who gave the claimed share must compensate from his own portion. Abu Yusuf compares this to claiming a common part in the whole property, which would nullify the division. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the purpose of division is to separate shares, and since the claim is limited to one partner's share, the division stands, analogous to the case where two partners divide property that includes a third's share in one part—that division is valid. The key distinction is between a claim affecting both shares (which would harm the third party) and one affecting only one share (no harm). The relied-upon position (al-aṣaḥḥ) is with Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqāq): A claim of ownership or right by a third party after a division has been made.
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property into separate shares.
شائع (shā'i'): An undivided share in a property, not yet separated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a third party claims a share that is common (shā'i') in only one partner's portion after division, what happens?
A) The division is rescinded entirely.
B) The division stands, and the partner must compensate the claimant.
C) The division stands without any compensation.
D) The division is rescinded only if the claimant objects.

Key Takeaway
A third party's claim confined to one partner's share after division does not invalidate the division; the partner compensates, upholding the purpose of separation (tamayyuz).

Muha'a'ah: Definition, Evidence, and Temporal Division of Usufruct
Comprehensive treatment of temporary division of usufruct with evidence and applications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define muha'a'ah, state its legal ruling and conditions, and distinguish between spatial and temporal division.

Core Idea
Muha'a'ah divides usufruct without dividing the property: permissible by istihsan, not qiyas.

Muha'a'ah is a vital concept in Hanafi property law, allowing co-owners to share the use of a jointly owned asset without physically splitting it. This lesson unpacks its definition, the istihsan-based evidence from Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, its conditions, and the two main types: spatial and temporal division. Understanding muha'a'ah equips you to handle modern co-ownership scenarios, such as shared family homes or rental properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Recognize that muha'a'ah is a division of usufructs (qismat al-manāfi'), as opposed to division of physical objects (qismat al-a'yān).
This is a type of qismah, but with unique rules.
2
Locate the evidence (dalīl)
Identify the three proofs: Quran (26:155), Sunnah (Battle of Badr camel-sharing), and Ijmāʿ. Understand why qiyas is abandoned.
The qiyas would forbid it as an exchange of benefit for its like (ribā), but istihsān allows it.
3
Understand the ruling and conditions
State that muha'a'ah is wājib when requested by one partner and no request for full division; otherwise mubāḥ. The property must be usable while its essence remains.
If one partner wants division, preference is given to division.
4
Distinguish spatial vs. temporal types
Spatial: complete segregation, no time limit needed, each can utilize their portion freely. Temporal: partial segregation, needs duration specification, treated as a loan of shares.
If partners disagree, judge chooses: spatial is more just, temporal more complete.
5
Apply to specific cases and note ikhtilāf
Consider applications: house, slaves, income. Note the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abū Ḥanīfa does not allow compulsion for slaves; the Ṣāḥibayn and muftā bihī allow it.
The relied-upon position is that the judge can compel muha'a'ah.

ولو تهايئا : التهايؤ في اللغة مشتق من الهيئة وهي الحالة الظاهرة للشيء، والتهايؤ تفاعل منها، وهو أن على أمر، فيتراضوا به، وحقيقته أن كلا منهم يرضى بهيئة واحدة ،ويختارها وفي الشرع: عبارة عن قسمة المنافع. ولما فرغ المصنف عن بيان قسمة الأعيان شرع في بيان قسمة المنافع؛ لكونها فرعا عليها، ويجري جبر القاضي فيها كما في قسمة الأعيان إلا أن القسمة أقوى في استكمال المنفعة؛ لأنه جمع المنافع في زمان واحد، بخلاف المهايأة، فإنها على التعاقب، ولهذا لو طلب أحدهما القسمة، والآخر المهايأة، يرجح الطالب للقسمة، ولو وقعت المهايأة فيما يحتمل القسمة، ثم طلب أحدهما القسمة، تفسخ وتقسم. يتواضعوا واعلم أن جواز المهايأة بالاستحسان، وكان القياس يأباه؛ لأنها مبادلة منفعة بجنسها؛ لأن كل واحد من الشريكين ينتفع في نوبته بملك شريكه عوضا عن انتفاع شريكه بملكه في نوبته، ولكن ترك القياس بالكتاب أعني قوله تعالى: لَهَا شِرْبٌ وَلَكُمْ شِرْبُ يَوْمٍ مَعْلُومٍ (الشعراء: (١٥٥) وبالسنة؛ إذ قد ورد عنه عليه في غزوة بدر أنه قسم كل بعير بين ثلاثة نفد، وكانوا يتهايئون في الركوب، وبإجماع الأمة على جوازها وشرطها أن تكون العين يمكن الانتفاع بها مع بقاء عينها، وصفتها: أنها واجبة إذا طلبها بعض الشركاء، ولم يطلب الشريك الآخر القسمة. (فتح، تكملة)  كتاب القسمة ٣٠١ مسائل القسمة في سكنى دار ودارين أو خدمة عبد أو عبدين أو غلة دار أو دارين صح المكان. في سكنى دار الخ: أي تهائيا في سكني دار بأن يسكن هذا بعضها، وهذا بعضها، أو يسكن هذا في العلو، وهذا في السفل، وهذا هو التهايؤ من حيث المكان، أو يسكن جميع الدار أحدهما شهرا، والثاني شهرا، وهذا هو التهايؤ من حيث الزمان، أو في سكنى دارين على أن يسكن كل واحد منهما دارا، وهذا أيضا من التهايؤ في واعلم أن التهايؤ إما أن يكون من حيث المكان أو من حيث الزمان، ففي الوجه الأول: التهايؤ إفراز من كل وجه، ولهذا لا يشترط فيه التوقيت، ولكل أن يستغل ما أصابه بالمهايأة، وإن لم يشترط لحدوث المنافع. وفي الوجه الثاني: إفراز من وجه ويجعل كالمستقرض لنصيب شريكه، ولو اختلفا في التهايؤ من حيث الزمان والمكان في محل يحتملهما كالدار مثلا يطلب أحدهما أن يسكن في مقدمها، وصاحبه في مؤخرها، والآخر يطلب أن يسكن جميع الدار ،شهرا، وصاحبه شهرا ،آخر يأمرهما القاضي بالاتفاق يعني على أحدهما؛ لأن التهايؤ في المكان أعدل، وفي الزمان أكمل، فلو اختاراه من حيث الزمان يقرع في البداءة بينهما تطييبا لقلوبهما، وينظر في قدر المدة (عيني، فتح بتوضيح خدمة عبد على أن يخدم هذا يوما وهذا يوما. (عيني) أو عبدين إلخ على أن يخدم هذا العبد هذا وهذا العبد هذا. (عيني)] وكذا تجوز المهايأة في خدمة عبد وأمة كما في 'الخانية'، فإن شرطا طعام كل عبد على من يخدمه جاز، وفي الكسوة لا يجوز؛ لأن العادة جرت بالمسامحة في الطعام دون الكسوة، ولقلة التفاوت في الطعام، وكثرته في الكسوة، ولو تمايئا في عبدين استخداما، فمات أحدهما أو أبق، انتقضت المهايأة. (فتح باختصار) أو غلة دار إلخ على أن يأخذ هذا شهرا وهذا شهرا. (عيني) ولو زادت غلة الدار الواحدة في نوبة أحدهما على الغلة في نوبة الآخر، يشتركان في الزيادة تحقيقا للتعادل، وعليه الفتوى كما في 'الخانية'، بخلاف ما إذا كان التهايؤ على المنافع، فاستغل أحدهما في نوبته زيادة؛ لأن التعديل فيما وقع عليه التهايؤ حاصل، وهو المنافع، فلا تضره زيادة الاستغلال والتهايؤ على الاستغلال في دارين جائز أيضا في ظاهر الرواية، ولو فضل غلة أحدهما لا يشتركان فيه بخلاف الدار الواحدة والفرق أن في الدارين معنى التمييز والإفراز راجح؛ لاتحاد زمان الاستيفاء بخلاف الدار الواحدة؛ لتعاقب وصول المنفعة، فاعتبر ،قرضا، وجعل كل واحد في نوبته كالوكيل عن صاحبه، فلهذا يرد عليه حصته من الفضل دارين على أن يأخذ هذا غلة هذه، وهذا غلة هذه. (عيني) صح إلخ: أي صح التهايؤ في هذه الوجوه الستة الأول: يجوز بالاتفاق؛ لأن القسمة على هذا الوجه جائزة، فكذا المهايأة، وقيل: يجوز عنده بالتراضي، ولا يجبر اعتبارا بالقسمة وعنه أنه لا يجوز التهايؤ أصلا لا بالجبر ولا بالتراضي؛ لأنه يصير بيع المنافع من جنسه نسيئة، وذلك لا يجوز، والثاني أيضا يجوز بالاتفاق، وكذا الثالث: يجوز بالاتفاق والرابع: يجوز على الأصح، وعند أبي حنيفة: لا يجوز إلا بالتراضي؛ لأن قسمة الرقيق لا يجري فيها الجبر عنده، فكذا منفعته، والأصح أن القاضي بهايئ بينهما جبرا بطلب أحدهما، والخامس: يجوز بالاتفاق، والسادس فيه خلاف والأظهر أنه يجوز بالاتفاق [رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٣/٢]
And if they mutually share (tahāyu'): linguistically, tahāyu' is derived from hay'a (state) which is the apparent condition of a thing, and tahāyu' is a mutual form, meaning they agree upon a matter, and its reality is that each of them is satisfied with one state and chooses it. In (Islamic) law, it refers to division of usufructs. When the author finished explaining the division of things (a'yān), he began explaining the division of usufructs because it is subsidiary to it. Compulsion by the judge applies in it as in division of things, except that division is stronger in completing the benefit because it collects usufructs in one time, unlike muha'a'ah, which is successive. For this reason, if one requests division and the other muha'a'ah, the one requesting division is given preference. And if muha'a'ah occurs in something that can be divided, and then one requests division, it (the muha'a'ah) is rescinded and (the property) is divided. Know that the permissibility of muha'a'ah is by istihsan, whereas qiyas would reject it because it is an exchange of benefit for its like, since each partner in his turn benefits from the other's property in exchange for the other benefiting from his property in his turn. But qiyas was abandoned due to the Book, namely His statement: 'For her is a drink and for you is a drink on a known day' (26:155), and due to the Sunnah: indeed it is reported from him (peace be upon him) in the Battle of Badr that he divided every camel among three riders, and they would take turns riding (yatahāya'ūn). And due to the consensus of the ummah on its permissibility. Its condition: the thing must be usable while its essence remains. Its description: it is obligatory if some partners request it and the other partner does not request division. (Fath, Takmilah) [PAGE_302] Book of Division 301 Issues of Division: Regarding residing in one house or two houses, or service of one slave or two slaves, or income of one house or two houses, it is valid. 'Regarding residing in a house, etc.' meaning they mutually shared in residing in a house such that one lives in part of it and the other in another part, or one lives on the upper floor and the other on the lower floor — this is tahāyu' with respect to place. Or one lives in the whole house for a month and the other for a month — this is tahāyu' with respect to time. Or regarding residing in two houses such that each lives in one house — this is also tahāyu'. Know that tahāyu' is either with respect to place or time. In the first aspect: tahāyu' is complete segregation, so timing is not stipulated, and each may utilize what he receives by muha'a'ah even if not stipulated due to the occurrence of benefits. In the second aspect: it is partial segregation and is treated as if one borrows the share of his partner. If they differ regarding tahāyu' by place or time in a location that can accommodate both, like a house: one wants to live in the front and the other in the back, and the other wants to live in the whole house for a month and the other for another month, the judge orders them to agree on one. Because tahāyu' by place is more just, and by time is more complete. If they choose by time, lots are cast for who begins, to make their hearts content, and consideration is given to the duration. ('Ayni, Fath with clarification) 'Service of a slave' on the condition that one serves him one day and the other the next. ('Ayni) 'Or two slaves, etc.' on the condition that this slave serves one and that slave serves the other. ('Ayni) Similarly, muha'a'ah in service of a male slave and a female slave is permissible as in al-Khaniyah. If they stipulate the food of each slave upon the one who uses him, it is valid; but regarding clothing it is not valid, because custom is lenient about food but not clothing, and there is little disparity in food but much in clothing. And if they mutually share in using two slaves, and one dies or runs away, the muha'a'ah is rescinded. (Fath, abridged) 'Or income of a house, etc.' on the condition that one takes it for a month and the other for a month. ('Ayni) If the income of a single house increases during one's turn over the income in the other's turn, they share in the increase to achieve equality, and upon this is the fatwa as in al-Khaniyah, unlike if the tahāyu' is on the usufruct itself and one utilizes more in his turn, because the adjustment is in what the tahāyu' was upon, i.e., the usufruct, so the increase in utilization does not harm him. Tahāyu' on the income of two houses is also permissible in the apparent riwāyah. If the income of one exceeds, they do not share in it, unlike a single house. The difference: in two houses, the meaning of distinction and segregation is predominant due to the unity of the time of extraction, unlike a single house due to the succession of receipt of benefit. So it is considered a loan, and each in his turn is like an agent for his partner, therefore he returns to him his share of the excess. 'Two houses' on the condition that one takes the income of this one and the other the income of that one. ('Ayni) 'Valid, etc.' i.e., the tahāyu' is valid in these six aspects: The first: allowed by agreement because division in this manner is permissible, thus muha'a'ah. It is said it is allowed by mutual consent but the judge does not compel, analogizing to division. And from him (Imam Muhammad?) that muha'a'ah is not allowed at all, neither by compulsion nor by consent, because it becomes a sale of usufructs of the same kind on credit, which is not allowed. The second is also allowed by agreement. Similarly the third: allowed by agreement. The fourth: allowed according to the most correct view. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not allowed except by mutual consent because division of slaves does not involve compulsion according to him, thus also for their usufruct. The most correct is that the judge orders them to do muha'a'ah by compulsion if one requests. The fifth: allowed by agreement. The sixth: there is disagreement, but the apparent view is that it is allowed by agreement. (Ramz al-Haqā'iq: 2/353)
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This extensive passage is a thorough treatment of muha'a'ah (temporary division of usufruct) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary. It begins by defining the term linguistically and legally: it is a division of usufructs, as opposed to division of physical objects (a'yān). The commentator explains that muha'a'ah is permissible by istihān (juristic preference), even though qiyas would forbid it because it involves exchanging a benefit for its like (ribā al-fadl). The proofs for istihsan are: (1) the Quranic verse about the she-camel and its drink, (2) the practice of the Companions in the Battle of Badr who took turns riding camels, and (3) consensus. A condition is that the property must be usable while its essence remains. The ruling: if one partner requests muha'a'ah and the other does not request division, it becomes obligatory (wājib) on the partner to agree. The passage then details the types: spatial (tahāyu' bi-al-makān) and temporal (tahāyu' bi-al-zamān). Spatial muha'a'ah is considered complete segregation, so no time limit is needed, and each can utilize his portion freely. Temporal muha'a'ah is considered a kind of loan of shares. If partners disagree on which type, the judge chooses; spatial is more just, temporal more complete. If temporal is chosen, lots are cast for who begins. The passage provides specific applications: housing (one house or two), service of slaves (one or two), and income of houses (one or two). For a single house's income, any excess in one turn is shared to maintain equality; for two houses, excess is not shared because the segregation is more complete. Regarding slaves, muha'a'ah is valid; if one dies or runs away, the agreement ends. The commentator also discusses clothing vs. food for slaves: food is customarily lenient, so it can be stipulated; clothing is not. Finally, there is a summary of six cases (the two types applied to three categories: house, slave, income) and the differences of opinion. Most cases are agreed upon, but there is dispute regarding slaves (Abu Hanifa only allows by mutual consent, but the relied-upon view is that the judge can compel).

Key Terms
مهايأة (muha'a'ah): Division of usufructs among co-owners, either by time or by space, without dividing the physical property.
تهايؤ (tahāyu'): Synonymous with muha'a'ah; the mutual agreement to share usufructs.
قسمة المنافع (qismat al-manāfi'): Division of benefits (usufructs) as opposed to division of physical objects (a'yān).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for muha'a'ah to be valid?
A) The property must be movable.
B) The property must be usable while its essence remains.
C) The partners must be equal in number.
D) The agreement must be in writing.

Key Takeaway
Muha'a'ah is a permissible temporary division of usufruct, supported by istihsan from Quran and Sunnah, with distinct rules for spatial and temporal arrangements.

Musaqah: Definition, Intra-Hanafi Dispute, and Four Distinctive Conditions
Definition, intra-Hanafi dispute, and four conditions of musaqah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define musaqah, state the intra-Hanafi dispute on its permissibility, and distinguish its four conditions from those of muzara'ah.

Core Idea
Musaqah is permissible via the Sahibayn; fatwa is on their view.

The contract of musaqah (irrigation contract) is a vital agricultural arrangement, yet its ruling in the Hanafi school involves a well-known internal disagreement. This passage defines musaqah, presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and then details the four conditions that set musaqah apart from muzara'ah. Understanding these nuances is essential for applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Define Musaqah Linguistically and Legally
Read the first part of the passage to extract the definition: a contract where trees are handed to a worker in exchange for a share of the fruit. Note its similarity to muzara'ah.
The term 'musaqah' comes from irrigation (saqy).
2
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Dispute and the Mufta Bihi
Locate the statement that musaqah is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa but is permissible according to the Sahibayn. Understand that the fatwa is on the latter view.
This is a classic example of ikhtilaf within the school with a clear tarjih.
3
Note the Four Distinguishing Conditions
The passage lists four exceptions where musaqah differs from muzara'ah. List them: (1) no compulsion if one party refuses, (2) no rent after expiry, (3) different compensation if trees are reclaimed, (4) period need not be specified by istihsan.
These conditions reflect practical flexibility.
4
Understand the Rationale for the Fourth Condition
Analyze why specifying the period is not required in musaqah: the ripening time is known and varies little, so ignorance is not gross. Contrast with muzara'ah where variation in crop cycles makes specification necessary.
This is an application of istihsan.

كتاب المساقاة تعريف المساقاة وحكمها مفاعلة من السقي لغة هي معاقدة دفع الأشجار إلى من يعمل فيها على أن الثمر بينهما، وهي كالمزارعة، الشرع المساقاة تصح في النخل والشجر والكرم والرطاب وأصول الباذنجان. فإن دفع نخلا فيه ثمرة أي المساقاة مساقاة، والثمرة تزيد بالعمل صحت، على وجه المساقات و الحال أن الثمرة كتاب المساقاة وجه المساقاة المناسبة بين الكتابين ظاهر؛ لأن كلا منهما عقد شرع لتحصيل منفعة الملك، ولهذا كانت كالمزارعة حكما وخلافا وشروطا إلا أن حق المساقاة كان أن تقدم على المزارعة؛ لكثرة من يقول بجواز المساقاة، ولورود الأحاديث في معاملة النبي عليه أهل خيبر، لكن قدم المزارعة؛ لشدة الحاجة إلى معرفة أحكامها، وكثرة تفاريع مسائلها. فتح بتصرف) وهي كالمزارعة إلخ يعني لا يجوز عند الإمام ويجوز عندهما، والفتوى على قولهما. وشروطها عندهما شروط المزارعة إلا في أربعة أشياء: أحدها: إذا امتنع أحدهما عن المضي لا يجبر ؛ لأنه لا ضرر عليه في المضي، بخلاف المزارعة على ما تقدم. الثاني: إذا انقضت المدة تترك بلا أجرة بخلاف المزارعة الثالث: إذا استحق النخل يرجع العامل بأجرة مثله، والمزارع بقيمة الزرع الرابع: في بيان المدة، فإذا لم يبين المدة فيها يجوز استحسانا؛ لأن وقت إدراك الثمرة معلوم، وقلما يتفاوت فيه، فيدخل ما هو المتيقن به وإدراك البذر في أصول الرطبة هذا بمنزلة إدراك الثمار؛ لأن لها نهاية معلومة، فلا يشترط فيها بيان المدة، بخلاف الزرع؛ لأن ابتداءه يختلف، والانتهاء يبتني عليه، فتدخله الجهالة الفاحشة
The book of Musaqah. Definition of Musaqah and its ruling. It is a verbal noun from irrigation in language. It is a contract of handing over trees to someone who works on them on condition that the fruit is shared between them, and it is like Muzara'ah. [Commentary: The appropriateness between the two chapters is apparent because each is a contract legislated to obtain benefit of property, and therefore it is like Muzara'ah in ruling, disagreement, and conditions, except that the right of Musaqah should have been presented before Muzara'ah because many say it is permissible and due to the hadiths of the Prophet's transaction with the people of Khaybar, but Muzara'ah was presented first due to the severe need to know its rulings and the abundance of its subsidiary issues. (From Fath with adaptation) 'And it is like Muzara'ah' etc. means it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa and is permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the fatwa is on their statement. Its conditions according to them are the conditions of Muzara'ah except in four matters: First: If one of them abstains from proceeding, he is not compelled, because there is no harm on him in proceeding, unlike Muzara'ah as previously. Second: If the period expires, it is left without rent, unlike Muzara'ah. Third: If the palm trees are claimed (by a third party), the worker takes the wage of his like, and the owner of the land takes the value of the crop. Fourth: Regarding the specification of the period: if the period is not specified in it, it is permissible by istihsan, because the time of ripening of the fruit is known and rarely varies, so what is certain enters (the contract). And the ripening of seeds in the roots of moist plants is like the ripening of fruits because they have a known end, so specifying the period is not required in them, unlike crops because their beginning varies and the end is built upon it, so gross ignorance enters.]
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage defines the contract of Musaqah (irrigation contract) and presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its permissibility. The author first gives the linguistic and legal definitions: it is a contract where trees are handed to a worker who tends them in exchange for a share of the fruit. Then he notes that Musaqah is similar to Muzara'ah (sharecropping) in many respects. The commentary explains that the chapter on Musaqah is placed after Muzara'ah despite its greater focus in hadith (e.g., the Prophet's transaction with Khaybar) because the need to understand Muzara'ah is more urgent due to its many subsidiary rulings. Then the key dispute is stated: Imam Abu Hanifa does not permit Musaqah, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it, and the fatwa is on their view. The Sahibayn's conditions for Musaqah are the same as those for Muzara'ah except in four specific points. First, if one party refuses to proceed, he is not forced to continue, because there is no harm in proceeding (unlike Muzara'ah where the owner may be forced to wait). Second, if the contract period expires, the land is left without rent (whereas in Muzara'ah, the owner may charge rent). Third, if the trees are claimed by a rightful owner, the worker gets his wage equivalent, and the landowner gets the value of the crop (in Muzara'ah, the worker gets wage, the owner gets crop value). Fourth, if the duration is not specified, Musaqah is valid by istihsan because the ripening time is known, whereas in Muzara'ah, specification is required due to potential variation. The passage thus clarifies the flexibility granted to Musaqah based on practical need and istihsan.

Key Terms
المساقاة (al-musāqāh): A contract where trees are handed to a worker who tends them in exchange for a share of the fruit.
المزارعة (al-muzāraʿah): Sharecropping contract where land is given to a cultivator for a share of the produce.
الإمام (al-imām): Refers to Imam Abu Hanifa, the founder of the Hanafi school.
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juridical preference; departing from strict analogy for a stronger reason (e.g., custom or need).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is one of the four differences between Musaqah and Muzara'ah?
A) In Musaqah, if one party refuses to proceed, he is compelled; in Muzara'ah he is not.
B) In Musaqah, if the period ends, the land is left without rent; in Muzara'ah, rent may be charged.
C) In Musaqah, the duration must always be specified; in Muzara'ah it may be vague.
D) In Musaqah, the worker gets no wage if trees are claimed; in Muzara'ah he does.

Key Takeaway
Musaqah is permissible in the Hanafi school on the Sahibayn's view, with four conditions differing from muzara'ah.

Validity of Musaqah in Various Trees and Associated Rulings
States the trees in which Musaqah is valid and explains rulings on termination, death, and defects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the trees in which Musaqah is valid according to the Hanafi school and explain the rulings on termination, death, and defects.

Core Idea
Musaqah is valid in all trees with stems; contract ends when fruit ripens, and is voided by death or valid excuses.

Musaqah is a special type of agricultural partnership where a worker tends trees in exchange for a share of the fruit. The Hanafi school, following the Sahibayn, permits this contract in all trees that produce fruit and have a stem, including palms, vines, reeds, and even eggplant roots. In this lesson, you will learn the scope of validity, the condition that fruit must increase with work, and the consequences of death, corruption, and valid excuses for termination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the valid trees for Musaqah
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Musaqah is valid in all trees that have a stem and produce fruit that increases with work. This includes palm trees, grapevines, reeds (moist plants), and eggplant roots. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa prohibited Musaqah entirely, but fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view.
The Shafi'i school restricts Musaqah to palm trees and grapevines, relying on the Hadith of Khaybar as a specific exception.
2
Understand the condition of fruit increase
Musaqah is only valid if the fruit is still capable of increasing with work. If the fruit has fully ripened (e.g., dates become ripe) and no longer grows, the contract is invalid. However, if the fruit only needs preservation (like guarding from theft), some scholars allow it.
The worker deserves wages only for actual work; once fruit is ripe, he can do no more, so the contract ends.
3
Analyze the effects of corruption and death
If the Musaqah contract is corrupt (fasid), the worker receives his wage equivalent (ajr al-mithl), not exceeding the agreed share. Death of either party nullifies the contract, but by istihsan, the worker (or his heirs) may continue until the fruit ripens to avoid hardship. The landowner's heirs cannot force the worker to stop.
Muhammad argues that the worker should get his wage equivalent regardless of the agreed share.
4
Examine valid excuses for rescission
The contract can be rescinded for valid excuses such as the worker being a known thief (before ripening) or becoming too sick to work. The landowner may also rescind if he is overwhelmed by debt and needs to sell the vineyard.
After the fruit ripens, no rescission is possible because the contract has effectively ended.

(ملخصا من الفتح) كالمزارعة إلخ : يعني إذا زارع الزرع، وهو بقل جاز، وإن أدرك واستحصد لم يجز. رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٨/٢] فللعامل أجر مثله لأنها في معنى الإجارة الفاسدة، ولا يزاد على ما شرط له من الثمرة، وقال محمد له أجر مثله بالغا ما بلغ ولم يذكر هذا الشرط اكتفاء بما قال في صدر الكتاب: وهي كالمزارعة"، وهذا الشرط في المزارعة مذكور. (ملا مسكين بزيادة يسيرة) وتفسخ بالعذر إلخ: أي تفسخ المساقات بالعذر كالمزارعة؛ لأنها في معنى الإجارة، وقد بينا أنها لا تفسخ بالأعذار، ثم عذر صاحب الكرم لحوق دين فادح لا يمكن وفاؤه إلا ببيع الكرم. (تكملة، فتح) بأن يكون إلخ: أي معروفا بالسرقة يعني من جملة الأعذار كون العامل سارقا يخاف عليه سرقة السعف والثمر قبل الإدراك؛ لأنه يلزم صاحب الأرض ضرر لم يلتزمه فيفسخ ،به وإنما قيدنا بقو: "قبل" الإدراك"؛ إذ بعد الإدراك انتهت فلا يمكن الفسخ ومن جملتها مرض العامل إذا كان يضعفه عن العمل؛ لأن في إلزامه استئجار الأجراء
'And it is valid in palm trees etc.' i.e., Musaqah is valid according to the two (Sahibayn) in all these things. Al-Shafi'i in his new opinion says: It is not permissible except in palm trees and grapevines, and Muzara'ah is not permissible except as subsidiary to Musaqah, such as when palm trees and grapevines are in white land irrigated with palm water, and he orders that the land also be planted with half share. His evidence in restricting permissibility to palm trees and grapevines is that its permissibility is based on the hadith of Khaybar, which is specific and thus cannot be extended, and that he (the Prophet) employed the people of Khaybar for half of what comes out of fruit or crop, narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and others. But this (hadith) is absolute, so it is not permissible to restrict it to some trees without others. Know that the word 'palm trees' was not taken by the commentators in the matn, nor is it in all printed copies, but it is in the Ahmad manuscript and was transmitted from it in this book. ... 'And if it ends, no' (i.e., if the fruit has ripened and does not increase by work, Musaqah is not valid because the worker does not deserve wages except by work, and there is no effect of work after completion. ... 'And if it becomes corrupt, the worker gets his wage equivalent.' ... 'And it is nullified by death' and 'it is rescinded for an excuse like Muzara'ah, such as the worker being a thief or sick unable to work.'
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage expands on the types of trees in which Musaqah is valid according to the Sahibayn (all trees with stems, including palm, grapevine, reeds, and eggplant roots) and contrasts with Shafi'i's view restricting it to palm and grapevine. The Hanafi response relies on the absolute hadith of Khaybar. The passage then discusses three specific rulings: (1) If the fruit has fully ripened and no longer grows with work, Musaqah is invalid because the worker cannot earn wages without work; an exception is made for trees needing only preservation. (2) If the contract becomes corrupt (fasid), the worker receives his wage equivalent (ajr al-mithl), and he cannot be given more than what was agreed upon for the fruit. (3) Termination: the contract is voided by death of either party, but by istihsan the worker (or his heirs) may continue until the fruit ripens to avoid hardship. If both die, the worker's heirs have the option to continue, not the landowner's heirs. Additionally, the contract can be rescinded for valid excuses (like the worker being a thief or too sick to work) before the fruit ripens; after ripening, no rescission is possible. The passage also mentions that the landowner's financial hardship (overwhelming debt) may justify rescission if he cannot pay except by selling the vineyard.

Key Terms
الرطاب (al-riṭāb): Plural of ratbah, meaning moist plants; here it refers to all kinds of vegetables/legumes that have stems, specifically including Egyptian 'barysam'.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The wage equivalent for similar work in the market, given to the worker when the contract is corrupt or terminated due to death.

D) Only in plants that require irrigation

Key Takeaway
Musaqah is valid in all trees with stems; the contract ends when fruit ripens, and is voided by death or valid excuses.

The Hanafi Ruling on Tasmiyah: Intentional vs Forgetful Omission
States ruling on tasmiyah and discusses ikhtilaf with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughter without tasmiyah (intentional and forgetful), explain the evidence from hadith, and apply the ruling to hunting and multiple-animal scenarios.

Core Idea
Tasmiyah is wajib; intentionally omitting it makes the meat haram, but forgetfulness is excused by hadith.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) during slaughter. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq distinguishes between intentional omission, which renders the meat haram due to consensus, and forgetful omission, which is excused by the prophetic hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان'. We will also explore why a rare earlier opinion from Imam Muhammad is rejected as a consensus-breaker, and how the ruling extends to hunting with dogs and arrows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is tasmiyah at the moment of slaughter. In Hanafi, it is wajib. Intentional omission → meat haram; forgetful omission → meat halal.
This is the default position from the matn.
2
Note the Scope of Companion Disagreement
The only ikhtilaf among Sahaba was over forgetfulness: Ibn Umar said it is haram; Ali and Ibn Abbas said it is halal. Hanafi adopts the latter view.
This shows that ijtihad is allowed only in forgetful case, not intentional.
3
Examine the Proof for Forgetfulness
The hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' (My ummah is forgiven for error and forgetfulness) provides clear textual evidence. The wajh al-dalalah is the explicit word 'النسيان'.
This hadith is ahad but its indication is qat'i.
4
Address the Maliki Objection
Malik argued from general Quranic commands (Quran 6:118,121) to require tasmiyah absolutely. Hanafi response: the hadith specifies (takhsis) the general command, and the Companion disagreement confirms that forgetfulness is excused.
The famous Maliki position actually agrees with Hanafi.
5
Apply the Principle to Branch Cases
For involuntary slaughter (hunting), tasmiyah is attached to the instrument; if the instrument changes, tasmiyah must be renewed. For voluntary slaughter, it is attached to the animal. The passage gives examples with dogs, arrows, and multiple sheep.
Study the furu' carefully: e.g., if you say Bismillah on a knife then switch knives, you must repeat tasmiyah.

هذه
وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا ترك التسمية عند إرسال البازي أو الكلب وعند الرمي، وإذا أضجع شاة وسمى ثم تركها وذبح شاة أخرى، وترك التسمية عليها لا يحل. ولو رمى سهما إلى صيد وسمى، فأصاب صيدا آخر، لو أخذ سكينا وسمى، ثم تركه وأخذ سكينا آخر، أو أرسل كلبه إلى صيد وسمى، فترك الكلب ذلك الصيد وأخذ غيره، حل في جميع . الصور. ولو ذبح تلك الشاة ثم ذبح أخرى بعدها، فظن أن تلك التسمية تكفيه لا يحل ولو سمى على سهم ثم رمى بغيره صيدا لا يؤكل، وإنما لا يجوز أكله هنا، وجاز في ما إذا أخذ سكينا وسمى ثم تركه وأخذ سكينا آخر؛ لأن التسمية في الذكاة الاضطرارية مشروعة على الآلة وقد تغيرت وفي الذكاة الاختيارية على المذبوح وهو لا على وهو لم يتغير. واعلم أن المسلم والكتابي في ترك التسمية سواء. (عيني، هداية وغيرهما) وحل لو ناسيا أي حل ذبيحة تارك التسمية، لو ترك التسمية حال كونه ناسيا، وقال مالك: لا يحل لما بينا، و: قوله عليه: "رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان"، ومشهور مذهبه كمذهبنا رمز الحقائق: ٣٦٠/٢]
Book of Slaughterings. Rulings of slaughter: intentionally, and permissible if forgetful, and disliked to mention with Allah's name other than Him, and to say at the time of slaughter: = Leaving the tasmiyah (in the active or passive construction). This statement from him is considered a breach of consensus. Indeed the disagreement among them was concerning one who leaves the tasmiyah forgetfully: the madhhab of Ibn Umar is that it is prohibited, and the madhhab of Ali and Ibn Abbas is that it is permissible. For this reason Abu Yusuf and the mashayikh said: The one who leaves the tasmiyah intentionally is not subject to ijtihad, so even if a judge judges the permissibility of its sale, his judgment is not executed, because it contradicts consensus. And what he narrated contradicts definitive evidence and consensus, so it is rejected. Or we say: it is interpreted as the case of forgetfulness. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:360). And based on this disagreement, if he leaves the tasmiyah when releasing the falcon or dog and when shooting, and if he lays down a sheep and says tasmiyah, then leaves it and slaughters another sheep and leaves the tasmiyah for it, it is not permissible. And if he shoots an arrow at game and says tasmiyah, and it hits another game, or if he takes a knife and says tasmiyah, then leaves it and takes another knife, or sends his dog to game and says tasmiyah, and the dog leaves that game and takes another, it is permissible in all these cases. And if he slaughters that sheep, then slaughters another after it, thinking that the first tasmiyah suffices for it, it is not permissible. And if he says tasmiyah on an arrow and then shoots another, the game is not eaten. But it is permissible in the case where he takes a knife and says tasmiyah, then leaves it and takes another knife, because tasmiyah in involuntary slaughter is prescribed upon the instrument and it has changed, while in voluntary slaughter it is upon the slaughtered animal and it has not changed. Know that the Muslim and the Kitabi are equal in leaving the tasmiyah. (Ayni, Hidaya etc.) And it is permissible if forgetful, i.e., the slaughtered animal of one who leaves the tasmiyah while forgetful is permissible. Malik said: It is not permissible for the reason we stated, and his statement عليه: 'My ummah is forgiven for error and forgetfulness', and the famous position of his madhhab is like ours. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:360)
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the ruling of leaving out the tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') during slaughter. It first distinguishes intentional forgetfulness. The matn states that if one intentionally leaves tasmiyah, the meat is not halal; but if forgetful, it is halal. The author then reports a consensus-breaker: Imam Muhammad's earlier statement that it is halal even intentionally is considered a breach of ijma', as the only valid disagreement among the Companions was about the forgetful case. Ibn Umar held it haram, while Ali and Ibn Abbas held it halal. Therefore, Abu Yusuf and later scholars ruled that intentional omission is not open to ijtihad, and any judge's ruling permitting its sale would be invalid. The proof for forgetfulness is the hadith 'My ummah is forgiven for error and forgetfulness'. The passage then provides branch cases: if one sends a hunting dog or falcon without tasmiyah, or shoots an arrow without it, or if one intends to slaughter one animal with tasmiyah but then slaughters another without renewing it, etc. The principle is that for involuntary slaughter (like hunting), tasmiyah is attached to the instrument; if the instrument changes (e.g., different knife or dog), a new tasmiyah is needed. For voluntary slaughter, it is attached to the animal; if the animal changes, tasmiyah must be renewed. It also states that Muslim and Kitabi (People of the Book) are equal in this ruling. Finally, it notes that Imam Malik disagrees with the Hanafi position on forgetfulness, but the famous position of his school aligns with the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah' before slaughter.
ذبيحة (dhabīḥah): An animal slaughtered according to Islamic law.
نسيان (nisyān): Forgetfulness; forgetting to say tasmiyah during slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a person forgets to say 'Bismillah' while slaughtering an animal?
A) The meat is halal because the Prophet said the ummah is forgiven for forgetfulness.
B) The meat is haram because the Quran commands mentioning Allah's name.
C) The meat is makruh tanzihi.
D) The ruling differs depending on whether the animal is a sheep or a goat.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, forgetting tasmiyah is excused by hadith, making the meat halal; intentionally omitting it violates consensus and makes the meat haram.

Place of Slaughter and Tasmiyah Rulings
Rulings on place of slaughter and tasmiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proper place for slaughter, identify the requirement of tasmiyah, and apply the Hanafi rulings to cases involving the trachea knot and phrasing of the takbir.

Core Idea
Slaughter is valid only between throat and collarbone; tasmiyah is wajib; the trachea knot does not affect permissibility.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rulings on the correct place for slaughter (dhabh) and the mandatory utterance of tasmiyah. We will examine the hadith proof, clarify the common misconception about the trachea knot, and learn the proper wording of the takbir to avoid invalidating the slaughter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditions
The act is slaughtering an animal. The conditions include the correct location (between halq and labbah) and the utterance of tasmiyah.
The text also discusses the permissibility of supplications before the tasmiyah.
2
Locate the proof
The text cites the hadith 'Ala inna al-dhakaata fi al-halq' (Verily slaughter is in the throat) reported by al-Daraqutni.
Additional rational evidence: the throat contains passages for breath, food, and blood.
3
Understand the evidence
Cutting in the throat maximizes blood drainage, which is the purpose of slaughter. This confirms the place as between halq and labbah.
Cutting above or below renders the meat unlawful.
4
Apply the ruling to edge cases
The knot of the trachea (uqda) is not a factor; what matters is cutting most of the jugular veins. The meat is permissible regardless of the knot's position.
Fatawa from Samarqand and other sources confirm this.
5
Resolve the common misconception
The belief that the trachea knot must be cut is a saying of the common people and not legally valid. The Hanafi position is clear.
Also discuss the correct phrasing of takbir (without waw) to avoid interrupting tasmiyah.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the place of slaughter and the tasmiyah. The author begins by stating that saying 'Allahumma taqabbal min...' before the tasmiyah and laying down the animal is permissible. The proper place for slaughter is between the throat (halq) and the collarbone (labbah). The commentator explains that laying down the animal is not disliked. The discussion then moves to the correct phrasing of the tasmiyah, emphasizing that the takbir should be said without the waw (and) to avoid interrupting the tasmiyah. The proof for the place of slaughter is the hadith: 'Verily, slaughter is in the throat' and the fact that the throat contains the passage for breath, food, and blood vessels, making it the most effective place to drain blood. Cutting above or below the designated area renders the meat unlawful. The fatwa from Samarqand and other sources clarify that the knot of the trachea (uqda) is not a consideration; what matters is cutting most of the jugular veins, so the meat is permissible even if the knot remains above or below.

الحلق (al-halq): The throat, specifically the area where the trachea and esophagus are located.
اللبة (al-labbah): The collarbone area, the top of the chest.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The utterance of 'Bismillah' before slaughter.

Required Parts to Cut and Permissible Tools
Rulings on the minimum required cuts and permissible tools for slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four throat organs involved in dhabh, explain the Hanafi minimum cut requirement, and apply the hadith to identify permissible and prohibited tools.

Core Idea
Cutting three of the four vital throat organs suffices for valid slaughter; any sharp tool is allowed except attached teeth and nails.

This lesson addresses the essential requirements for the act of slaughter (dhabh) according to the Hanafi school. You will learn which parts of the animal's throat must be cut, the minimum number required, and the tools that may be used. The rulings are derived from authentic hadith and the Hanafi usul principle that the majority stands for the whole.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four organs
The text mentions al-mari' (esophagus), al-halqum (trachea), and al-wadajan (two jugular veins). Recognize these as the parts that may need to be cut.
The hadith uses the term awdaj (jugulars) to refer to all four.
2
Determine the minimum cut
The matn states that cutting three of the four is sufficient. This is the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf initially required specific organs.
The principle of akthar (majority) standing for the whole is applied.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Shafi'i holds that only trachea and esophagus need to be cut; Maliki requires all four. The Hanafi response is that the hadith mentions 'awdaj' and the purpose of blood flow is better achieved with an additional cut.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafi requires at least one jugular.
4
Identify permissible tools
The hadith 'Cause the blood to flow with whatever you wish' permits any sharp object that effectively cuts, except an attached tooth or nail. The exception is based on another hadith.
Detached teeth and nails are allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[رمز الحقائق: ٣٦٢/٢] إلا سنا وظفرا قائمين: أي متصلين بموضعهما ، يعني يجوز الذبح بكل ما أنهر الدم ولا يجوز بالسن والظفر القائمين؛ لقوله عليها في حديث رافع بن خديج: "أما السن فعظم، وأما الظفر فمدى الحبشة"، رواه البخاري، وتأويله إذا كان قائما يدل عليه قوله عليه: "أما الظفر فمدى الحبشة"؛ لأنهم كانوا يذبحون بالقائم. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٦٢/٢]
And the place of slaughter: the esophagus, the trachea, and the two jugular veins. Cutting three is sufficient, even with a nail, horn, bone, detached tooth, a piece of reed, a sharp stone, or anything that causes blood flow except a tooth and nail that are attached. [...]
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the essential parts to cut in dhabh and the tools that may be used. The matn states that the required cut is of three out of four: the esophagus (mari'), trachea (halqum), and one or both jugular veins (wadajan). Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that cutting three of the four suffices, while Abu Yusuf initially required cutting the esophagus, trachea, and one jugular. Imam Shafi'i considers cutting the esophagus and trachea enough, as the animal cannot survive after that. Imam Malik requires cutting all four. The Hanafi proof is that the majority (akthar) stands in place of the whole, as the purpose—blood flow (inhar al-dam) and quickening death (tawhiyah)—is achieved. Regarding tools, the hadith 'Cause the blood to flow with whatever you wish' permits any object that effectively causes blood flow, except a tooth or nail that is still attached (qa'im). The argument is that a tooth is bone and a nail is the knife of the Abyssinians, which is disliked. Detached teeth and nails are allowed, as they are not attached to a living body.

Key Terms
المريء (al-mari'): The esophagus, the passage for food and drink.
الحلقوم (al-halqum): The trachea, the passage for breath.
الودجان (al-wadajan): The two jugular veins; the blood vessels in the throat.
السن القائم (al-sin al-qa'im): An attached tooth that is still in the mouth.
الظفر القائم (al-zufr al-qa'im): An attached nail that is still on the finger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Halal, because any tool that causes blood flow is allowed.
B) Haram, because the nail is attached and considered a tool of the Abyssinians.
C) Makruh but permissible.
D) Permissible only if the nail is detached.

Key Takeaway
For valid Hanafi slaughter, three out of the four throat organs must be cut, and any sharp tool is permissible except an attached tooth or nail.
